<owt>
<txt id="zy/BT0uES0+MjcTHPoSx0Q" >
<lbl reserve="408" >When a new item type and quantity is entered into the register, the register looks up the product from the product catalog (using the Universal Product Code as an identifier), then adds the item and quantity as a sale line item in the collection of sale line items in the total sale.  If the item is the first item in the sale, the register first creates a new sale to hold the collection of sale line items.</lbl>

<not id="fRqLOLvp4UWjvefK3CJNLA" >
<dsc>Vector.elements( ) returns an object that implements the Enumeration interface</dsc>
<rlt>
<nta id="x/OG07tPl0GroAngUYnvug" >
<noe>
<RMS:LRF id="4FWp1ZZ+MEG9yabAZgzhLA" />
</noe>
</nta>
</rlt>
</not>
<not id="lgNk18BoiEy7Ub9P+49XDQ" >
<dsc reserve="292" >This is a &quot;not quite&quot; correct model of the reality of Java type casting.  The Java code takes the enumeration element and casts it as a SaleLineItem so we can send it the subtotal( ) message.  In a UML design model, we would just show a simple collection and not show details of type casting.</dsc>
<rlt>
<nta id="9gUYIpE010+3mwH8e2SD1g" >
<noe>
<RMS:LRF id="OqSam6geCUOh8hL09aIz5A" />
</noe>
</nta>

<not id="oSq5YEit0E2EeZmH8V8ghA" >
<dsc>Note</dsc>
</not>
</own>
<owt>
<txt id="Tgs5XicRmEWF7DPMvkwWDg" >
<lbl>increment total</lbl>
</txt>
<txt id="SsdRmDK0rkOD8suZkzlkTA" >
<lbl>For each element, get the subtotal and add it to the total.</lbl>
</txt>
<txt id="VJyLmsTCl067cnemCPiaQg" >
<lbl reserve="320" >Accept payment at the end of a sale.  The Sale is a Vector of SaleLineItems.  Each line item's subtotal is the item price times the quantity of the item.  The sale total is the sum of the subtotals.  The register should display to the clerk the amount of change:  the balance of the amount tendered minus the sale total.</lbl>
</txt>
</owt>
</dgx>
</owd>
